text:
This is a great recipe, but if this is your first time making cheesecake some of the basics are assumed.  A couple of notes for "first-timers"... make sure you read the Cheesecake Tips section of this board.  This recipe doesn't tell you some of the cheesecake fundamentals like 1) Make sure your cream cheese is at room temp before you start  2)Your batter should be smooth and silky.  If it is lumpy your cheesecakes will turn out badly.  If needed, throw the batter in a blender/food processor to get rid of the lumps  3)You do NOT want to wait for your cheesecakes to crack before removing them from the oven.  They are done before they crack, when the center is still soft.

After I learned these lessons, the recipe turned out well!

text:
These are delicious as is, but I made three different flavors using this batter with tremendous success and professional GOURMET looking results!
White Chocolate Red Raspberry: mixed 1/2 cup melted white chocolate into 1/3 of the batter, swirled 1/4 cup raspberry coulis into batter before fillig muffin cups and once baked I topped each with 1/2 teaspoon warmed seedless raspberry jam and drizzled melted white chocolate over the tops.
Chocolate Chip - substituted crushed oreos for nilla wafers, added 1/2 cup mini chocolate chips to 1/3 of batter, once baked topped with 1/2 teaspoon chocolate ganache.
Cherry Almond - substituted graham cracker crumbs for nilla wafers, added 1/2 teaspoon almond extract 1/3 batter and 1/2 teaspoon almond extract to cherry pie filling.  Once baked, topped each with 1 teaspoon sweetened sour cream topping (1/2 cup sour cream + 2 tbsp sugar + 1/2 teas vanilla extract) 2-3 cherries and sliced almond.
Feel free to email me at mpcharvat@yahoo.com for coulis, ganache or any other info.  Thanks!

I give this a 5 for the ingredients, but for me, these steps work better: I use regular muffin tins and I just put a vanilla wafer (flat side down) in the paper cup.  First, I whip the softened cream cheese until it is light and fluffy.  Then I gradually add the two eggs and vanilla and sugar at the end.  The mix seems to be very runny, but it turns out perfectly.  It takes longer to cook; I just keep an eye on the cheesecakes after about 20 minutes.

This recipe is AWESOME. i doubled it and used oreo crumbs instead of wafers. i  mixed all the abtter and i omitted vanilla extract. whn the batter was smooth i separated it itnto 3 bowls. to one bowl i added 2 tbls of creme de menthe, to the other bowl i added 2 tbls bailey's irish cream, to the last bowl i added 2 tbls Kahluah cofee liquer. i thought that i had maybe ruined the recipe by adding too much liquid, but it was PERFECT. i baked them for exactly 15 mins, they didnt crak and i took tem out right awy. rmeebr, these are just little guys, they dont need to sit in the oven and firm up like a big cheesecake. if you over cook them their creamy texture will disappear!
once they cooled, i added melted dark choc to the top of each one and to the kahluah ones i added a choc covered coffee bean, to the mint one si sprinkled crushed candy canes, and to the irish ones i added a green M&M.
Oh yes! i almost forgot
I used 2 cups of the choc cookie crumbs to which i added 4 tbls melted butter.
ALSO: leave your cream cheese out of the friegde for a good 4 hours b4 u start. i put mine beside the water heater to speed things up!!
use a MIXER...blend and blend and blend..mix all the cream cheese up until its super silky, THEN add the sugar, THEN after that add each egg one at a time
don't just plop it all in together.
exxxxxxxxxxcellent.

text:
Fabulous recipe!  So simple!  I have only made plain cheesecakes one time.   I have altered the recipe to make white chocolate raspberry, carmel, peanut butter, turtle, and strawberry.  I am getting very creative w/flavors and will someday have a list to rival the Cheesecake Factory! : )

I used fresh fruit for the raspberry and then preserves for the strawberry.  I find the ones w/fruit take about twice as long to bake.  The peanut butter has probably been the biggest hit out of all the flavors!  I just made the plain, peanut butter, turtle, and strawberry for a wedding reception (I made about 200 of them).  They were gobbled up within moments!  This recipe is definately a keeper!  

Some tips- 
I've used both the little mini muffin pans and normal muffin pans.  I prefer mini, but I think it really helps if you use muffin liners.  I used a water bath the 2nd time I used this recipe, and am not sure if it made a difference, except by making my oven feel 4 times hotter!  I'd like to think it made a difference, so I will do it again.  Garnishing these little bite sized beauties really sets them off and it's also very fun!  You can't go wrong w/this recipe.  

Please let me know if anyone wants details on the specific flavors I used and how I made them.  Happy baking!

text:
This is an easy, fun recipe for cheesecake, but it needs more precision.  There are two sizes of "mini" pan liners:  1 5/8" and 2". Half the recipe makes 24 mini cheesecakes in my mini muffin (tassie) pans.  Half the recipe makes 16 individual cheesecakes in 2" liners, freestanding on a baking sheet. I used about 8 vanilla wafers to make crumbs for the mini size and about 16 for the individual size.  In a 2" pan liner you can drop in a whole wafer instead.

text:
Easy recipe for your basic cheesecake filling. previous reviewers make an important notation when doing any type of cheesecake filling to include this recipe. Cream cheese needs to be at room temp. Put in mixing bowl and beat cream cheese by itself for about 4 minutes. It will be smooth and creamy, fluffy looking. THEN add the sugar, fist 1/2 cup and beat for about 3 mins. Taste. If you like it sweeter, add 1/4 c and beat about 3 more mins. Taste. If the creamed filling tastes kinda gritty from the sugar beat another 2 mins. You want the sugar blended into cream cheese really well. THEN add one egg, beat for 1 min, add second egg and beat for 1 min. Third egg is not neccessary. Omit vanilla. Use 1 tsp of lemon juice instead and beat for 2 mins. Taste. You may want an additional tsp of lemon juice depending on the taste you are looking for. At this point your filling should be really fluffy and smooth. If it's not beat for another 2 to 3 mins on med high speed. It will fluff. Use whatever crust you want but bind it with melted butter and lightly press into cups. I used regular cupcake pan and baked for 20 mins. Cool for about 20 mins after cooking. With a small teaspoon spoon out a small amount of cheesecake from center of  filling, creating a hole. Spoon in any pie filling you desire, lemon, cherries, stwberry, blberry, rasberry, ect. Put in fridge for several hours before serving.

text:
Way back in the '70s a co-worker brought these to a Christmas potluck. This recipe was new back then, of course, and everyone marveled just at the sight of them! One bite and we were all hooked. Once she shared the recipe we were all so surprised at how easy they were to make! These are so pretty, so easy, and just delicious. No need to crush the vanilla wafers if you use a standard muffin tin-- just drop a whole wafer in each cup. Over the years I've put my creative juices to work for endless variations...Oreo cookies or other cookies for the crust, lime juice or different extracts for the cheesecake filling, or chocolate and caramel sauce, fresh fruit and glaze for the topping, etc. These come together in mere minutes, are foolproof, and impressive on a beautiful serving platter.

I can't believe how wonderfully these turned out!  It was my first chance to make cheesecake of any type, and now I can't wait to try for the real thing.  

I followed other reviews and made my crust out of 2 cups graham cracker crumbs, 1 stick melted butter, and 8 tablespoons sugar.  I put about a half tablespoon in each liner.  They baked up beautifully, and were really easy!  

I made 2 batches of 48 mini cheesecakes each. I left 24 plain, topped 24 with strawberry pie filling, 24 with blueberry pie filling, and then did 24 with chopped pecans, mini chocolate chips, and drizzled caramel over the top.  I used the Kraft caramel bits.  So easy and the looked great!

text:
It was so easy to make and it was completed in such a short time!! I used oreo cookies instead of the wafers, ommitted the vanilla extract to suit the whole chocolate theme, and used M&Ms as topping. You just have to make sure that the batter is smooth and silky when done. Also, remember to blend the cream cheese (Room temperature please! Not fresh from the fridge!!) first, THEN add the sugar, THEN the eggs one at a time (Don't throw them in all at once). Try not to have any lumps of cheese left unblended. When baking, set the baking tray in another tray of BOILING HOT water (Hence the baking time remains the same) so that the base of the crust won't be burnt! You can also line the tray of water with a thick cloth. (Make sure the water doesn't overflow into your tray of cakes!) Finally remember not to overbake these little ones! Bake til set; the centre will still be soft though. Then you can switch off the oven and let them cook further in the remaining heat. Those are the main points for me but you can read all about it in the tips for cooking cheesecakes. My colleagues loved them...Great recipie!! =)

I followed someone else's suggestions and did the following.  I used oreo crumbs instead of wafers. i mixed all the batter and i omitted vanilla extract. whn the batter was smooth i separated it into 2 bowls. to one bowl i added 1 tbl of creme de menthe and green food coloring, to the other bowl i added 1 tbl bailey's irish cream. i baked them for exactly 15 mins i took tem out right away. They're small and if you over cook them their creamy texture will disappear! I used 1 cup of the choc cookie crumbs to which i added 2 tbls melted butter.
 ALSO: leave your cream cheese out of the fridge for a good 4 hours before you start or slightly microwave. Use a MIXER...blend and blend and blend..mix all the cream cheese up until its super silky, THEN add the sugar, THEN after that add each egg one at a time. Don't just plop it all in together.

text:
I've been making these for years.  Except my recipe calls for 1/2 c. sugar.  And I make them in the normal size cupcake pans which ends up making 24.  We prefer that to the mini because you get more of a cheesecake cookie instead of a sampler.  Also, it's just as easy to put a whole wafer cookie in the bottom vs. crumbs.  DON'T do as the video does by putting your filling on the top before you take them out of the pan.  That can only be MESSY.  I put mine in a container, store them in the frig. and put the pie filling on top before serving. Also, beat real good the cream cheese by itself, then beat it again when adding sugar and vanilla.  Then beat again when adding the eggs.  You will love the results of the batter.  I find 18 minutes is done in my gas stove/oven.  Hope you can utilize my tips.

text:
This recipe is wonderful! I used a few of the variations that I read in other reviews: ****** Peanut Butter - 1/4 of the batch of cheesecake batter, 2 tbs peanut butter, added three peanut butter chips to the top after I pulled them from the oven but while they were still hot, and drizzled melt chocolate on top after cooled ****** Almond - 1/4 batter - 1/2 teas almond extract in batter, 1/2 teas almond extract on some cherry pie filling, bake and when cool add cherries to the top ****** Chocolate - 1/4 cheesecake batter, I did not measure the cocoa powder or the melted chocolate (melted chips in the microwave) but added it little by little until batter had a nice medium brown color, drizzled white chocolate and milk choclate on top after cooled. ****** Chocolate Chip - I just took the regular batter and after I filled the muffin pan I added some mini choclate chips on top and baked ****** I did use a graham cracker crust for all of them (2 cups graham cracker crumbs, 8 tbl melted butter, 8 tbl sugar and mix) but next time I am going to try a oreo crust on the peanut butter and the choclate ones. ****** They did stick alittle to the paper liners so I will try tin foil type liners next time so I can remove the liners for presentation. I am also excited to try and make a turtle cheesecake type next round!     Thanks for the wonderful recipe! It was a major hit in the office!

Tasty and delicious! My boyfriend could not stop eating the! They were easy enough to make, being that it was my first time attempting "cheesecake." I made sure that my cream cheese was room temperature and that my batter was lump-free but not overbeat. I read that I should use a "water bath" for better results. Hmm. Tried it and I think it made a difference, cooked more evenly and they did not poof up. But, I felt like the batter was pretty runny still so I put them back in the oven for another 5 minutes. Took them out, chilled them and ta-da! Perfection. With my second batch I used no water bath and put them in for 20 minutes and they puffed up and sank a little in the middle. But, still delicious! I'm still learning, one day soon I shall master "cheesecake." In the meantime, my boyfriend's gonna keep eating them anyway!! And so will I! Thanks for this great recipe.

text:
It tastes delicious, but for them to come out just right, I had to follow these tips: 1.) If using foil muffin liners (regular size, as I don't have a mini muffin pan), bake for only 11-12 minutes max, any longer and the cheesecakes start to crack. 2.) Make sure cream cheese is at room temp. Then, whip cream cheese first to smooth, silky texture, no lumps. Then mix all other ingredients in separate bowl. Then gradually blend into cream cheese. 3.) I wanted a graham cracker crust - 2 cups crackers (2 pkgs), 8 T butter, 8 T sugar. Mix with hands. 4.) 1 heaping T of crust at bottom of cups, then pressed; then fill about 1/2 way - 3/4 way up with the cream cheese batter.

text:
Excellent cheesecakes. Why use a more complicated recipe when these turn out so well?

They're easy to personalize, too.

I divided the main cheesecake mix into smaller bowls and made the following flavors for holiday gifts:

Hot chocolate-I added a packet of hot cocoa mix to the batter, then after it was baked I added a dab of marshmallow fluff to the top and sprinkled it with some more powder for looks. Used a graham cracker crust.

Candy Cane- Used a chocolate graham cracker crust. After baking, I sprinkled crushed candy can bits on top.

Reese's PB cup- Using a choc grahm cracker base, I mixed half and half PB and cheesecake mix and baked. They baked faster than the others, so if you try this keep an eye on them. Also, the finish doesn't look as nice cause it doesn't smooth out while cooking, but it tastes great! It's disguised easily by drizzling with some melted chocolate.

Butterfinger- Crushed up some Butterfinger and sprinkled it on top of "plain" cheesecakes.

text:
Oh my gosh!! To die for!! But one glitch..I really hate to add suggestions others recipes because it's not mine to change but one the cream cheese NEEDS to be room temperature or your mix will be lumpy and not right. And you need to fluff your cream cheapest first *not* add everything all at once. Then lastly, I just couldn't go through with using the crust they suggested. Personally I like vanilla waffer crust better so this recipe was perfect but....no no no you can't leave the cookie crumbs as is, it will. Or hold it's shape as well and will taste sort of bland. I added ingredients to make it more of a crust like texture and with more taste. *This is used to make 14 crusts* first crush 20 Waffers to a very fine consistency, then add 2 and 1/4 tsp of granulated sugar, lastly combine with 2 tbs *melted* unsalted butter. Then fill each slot in the pan with some of the crust bake it on 350degrees for *5* minutes, take it out fill it with the cheese cake filling and bake it and your good to go! Hope this helps for those of you who are like me and prefer a vanilla waffer crust to a graham crust! Enjoy! (: ~Also I'm from Brooklyn NY originally so I have tasted some delicious cheese cake but trust me *if done right* these are delicious!~

text:
very yummy :) made this with my sister - super easy recipe! I made sure the cream cheese and eggs were at room temp (keep it out on the counter at least 4 hours)- once it was at room temp we mixed the cream cheese til there were no lumps and added the sugar - 2 eggs (one at a time - make sure it is well incorporated before adding the second egg) then added the rest of the ingredients.. we made sure not to overmix.. for the crust I used 1.5 cups of crushed graham crackers,1/4 cup of melted butter, 1/2 tsp of cinnamon and a little nutmeg .. baked in a waterbath at 350 for 18 minutes..turned the oven off and let cool in the oven for 10 minutes - then cooled on the counter until fully cool and refrigerate for a few hrs or overnight!

text:
YUM! I read A LOT of the reviews and took the top tips to make mine. Made the regular cupcake size (3 bites!). I brought my cream cheese to room temp (left on countertop overnight), made graham cracker crust (2 1/2 pkgs of graham crackers to make 2 cups, melted butter, 4ish TBSP brown sugar, 3ish TBSP white sugar, mixed up in the bag I crushed the grahams in, then packed into each cup with a shot glass (great idea!))while oven preheated to 350. Blended each ingredient as I added (first blended the cream cheese til it was workable,then added sugar (little less than 1/2c), blended, added about a tsp lemon juice (in place of vanilla), mixed, then added 2 eggs, blended). It was very smooth & silky when all the ingredients were finally together. Then spooned cheesecake to almost top of each cup. (This recipe makes one cupcake pan plus probably another half). Put these pans on top of pans that have walls, added water to these once in the oven for the waterbath.Baked for about 20 mins. Then turned off the oven and let it sit for 30 more mins in the oven. Took it out (no sunken cheesecake - they were beautiful!), cooled it, added cherry topping (2-3cherries per cupcake seems just enough). I tasted one then & it was alright but the graham crust crumbled. Put it in the fridge overnight and half a day, tried another one at lunch-and OMG DELICIOUS! The flavors melded & the crust stays together! I feel like a gourmet baker now (shhh)! woohoo!

I love these on so many levels! They are so easy, so quick and most importantly, SO good. If you have any experience making cheesecake, you know it takes time and attention and well worth it. I made these as directed, and by following the cheesecake making tips on this site. . My concern was the "crust". I couldn't understand how those crumbs would stick together, but I figured they had to if people didn't complain about it in their reviews. I was pleased to find that the loose crumbs do stick together just fine, phew! I made about 100 of these (that's how many paper liners I bought anyway) for a holiday party. I baked these in a water bath for 15 minutes and then turned off the oven and left them in it to cool for another 10 minutes.  Once that was done, I set the mini muffin pan on a wire rack for them to set up before transfering to the fridge for about an hour.  They turned out perfect-no cracks and no sinking tops. I gave it 4 stars due to my changes with the crust and cooking method.

What a delightful little recipe! I like to make them all different. I use slightly less sugar and the recipe turns out great. I have also used splenda, and stevia, with great results. You can substitute oreos for the wafers.  To make other flavors, add what you want! This recipe is very forgiving. For example, I made a kahlua version of this. text:
I made these for my class reunion and they turned out perfect. The recipe made exactly 48 mini-cakes. The vanilla wafers turned out well and tasted good, but my personal preference is a graham crust. I twisted the topping as other reviewers did. I topped half with fresh blueberries and drizzled with melted dark chocolate. The other half I used fresh rasberries and drizzled with melted white chocolate. If you try this, I suggest place the fruit on the cakes as soon as the come out of the oven to help the fruit settle and prevent it from rolling around. Also, if they are going to sit out for a while before eating, freeze them and then take out about 20 minutes before serving if you can.

I tried this with a few changes and it was really good! I'm sure it's great exactly as is too! I like pecans in my crust so I used the crust from the "Pumkpin Cheesecake II" recipe on this site by Cathy - (Combine 3/4 cup graham cracker crumbs, 1/2 cup ground pecans, 2 tablespoons white sugar, 2 tablespoons brown sugar, and 1/4 cup melted butter or margarine and mix well).. I made a batch of filling as is in this recipe, another batch with "White Chocolate Raspberry Cheesecake" recipe by CindyAnn for filling (same pecan/graham cracker crust I mentioned earlier), and a third batch with filling from "Chocolate Cappuccino Cheesecake" recipe by Cigdem Buke Ugur (with an oreo crust). Everyone seemed to enjoy the "White Chocolate Raspberry" one the most!

My co-worker (grandma, and former school teacher) gave me a cheese cupcake recipe that uses Nilla Wafers.  I lost the recipe, so I went looking for the next best thing.  Her recipe involved putting everything in a blender, eggs, Cheese, sugar and just slowly pulsing till it creamed together.  Since I didn't have Nilla Wafers, I used ginger snap cookies that I still had in the cupboard.  I still did the blender thing, so it's a one-blender recipe. Cooked for more than 15 minutes - more like 30 mins.  The cheesecake doesn't really get brown though, so don't overcook it. Blueberry or Cherry - Yummy!

text:
I followed the recipe exactly, using room temp cream cheese.
My batter never really appeared "light and fluffy", even with the Kitchen Aide mixer, but there were no problems with lumps.
I baked them for about 12 minutes, then turned off the oven and let them rest for 10 minutes before removing from oven.  I did not do a water bath because of the size of my muffin tin.
Cakes were lightly browned and did not crack.
The vanilla wafer crumbs worked fine, too. The cakes came out of the wrappers
without much mess and the crust held together.  I made 48 mini muffin-sized cakes and had a very little bit of batter left over.
I topped half with cherry pie filling and half with sugared pecans (1/2 C. chopped pecans, 1/2 C. brown sugar, 2 Tbsp. of butter, heated in skillet 'til sugar is dissolved) and chocolate chips.
They turned out very pretty and were popular at a party, but I just didn't care for the taste.
They reminded me of cheap, storebought cheesecake - sweet, but just not rich enough.  They also seemed a little "egg-y" for my tastes, and the crust and cherry topping seemed to overpower the tiny bite of cheesecake.
Like many sugar cookie recipes, these seem to be more for creating a pretty, decorative final product than for creating something you would really enjoy eating.
They are visually appealing and fun to make, so I would possibly suggest them for large parties, catering events, etc.  They might also be a good treat for children to help make and take to school for a party.

Here are the best:  add melted caramel to the top of each mini vanilla wafer.  Then add the cream cheese filling.  After they are baked, add melted chocolate and crumbled Heath bar to the tops.  The next best flavor was white chocolate raspberry.  I used this idea from another reviewer and added melted white chocolate to the batter.  After baking I added raspberry jam and a white chocolate chip to the top.  They were delicious!

text:
These are delicious as is, but I made three different flavors using this batter with tremendous success and professional GOURMET looking results! White Chocolate Red Raspberry: mixed 1/2 cup melted white chocolate into 1/3 of the batter, swirled 1/4 cup raspberry coulis into batter before fillig muffin cups and once baked I topped each with 1/2 teaspoon warmed seedless raspberry jam and drizzled melted white chocolate over the tops. Chocolate Chip - substituted crushed oreos for nilla wafers, added 1/2 cup mini chocolate chips to 1/3 of batter, once baked topped with 1/2 teaspoon chocolate ganache. Cherry Almond - substituted graham cracker crumbs for nilla wafers, added 1/2 teaspoon almond extract 1/3 batter and 1/2 teaspoon almond extract to cherry pie filling. Once baked, topped each with 1 teaspoon sweetened sour cream topping (1/2 cup sour cream + 2 tbsp sugar + 1/2 teas vanilla extract) 2-3 cherries and sliced almond. Feel free to email me at mpcharvat@yahoo.com for coulis, ganache or any other info. Thanks!  Bake 20mins in cupcake pan

This was my first baked cheesecakes, and while I know they aren't like doing the real thing, they turned out AMAZING!  I added white chocolate to half the batter and put raspberry jam on top after baking and cooling.  To the other half of the batter, I added semi-sweet chocolate and added finely ground coffee to the vanilla wafer crumbs.  (I ground my vanilla wafers and added butter and sugar to make the crusts)  They were delicious and simple.  They are time-consuming, for sure, but totally worth it.  Thanks for this easy recipe! UPDATE: I made this recipe last night but doubled it to use for a large cheesecake.  I added almost a whole bag of melted semi-sweet chocolate chips to the batter.  I think there is nothing this recipe can't do.  The cheesecake is wonderful.  Almost TOO good.  I made my own graham cracker crust and added coffee to it again. text:
I needed a recipe for a graduation party.  I read this recipe plus alot of the reviews.  I decided to make 4 batches.  Cherry cheesecake with graham cracker crust then with oreo cookie crust, white chocolate/raspberry with graham cracker crust and chocolate with oreo cookie crust.  With the white chocolate and chocolate I used 1/2 cup sugar and 1/2 cup melted chips.  When these were cooled and after I put seedless raspberry jam on the white chocolate.  I put a few of each chips in baggies, melted them, put a hole in the corner and drizzled a few lines with one color and with the other color I put the graduates initial over that.  I had the regular cupcake pans.  I put the batter in a gallon size zip lock bag, cut a hole in the corner and was able to get 24 cheesecakes with each recipe.  Remember to also use a toothpick to check if it is done.  Also one person said to make sure the cream cheese is room temp.  I left it out an hour and that wasn't long enough.  The next batch I waited for a total of two hours and that was perfect.  I had fun with this recipe.  Can't wait to try other suggestions that were given.

text:
I would have given this five stars except I didn't test the EXACT recipe.  I made these alterations:  I did a graham cracker crust instead of the vanilla wafers (1.5 cups graham cracker crumbs, 1/4 cup sugar, and 1/4 c. melted butter/margarine, all mixed together) and I added 1 T. flour to the cream cheese mixture (as most cheesecake recipes have a little flour).  I would also recommend refrigerating the cheesecakes (once cooled) before adding the cherry pie filling.  This recipe made more than 48 (about 60).  Overall, very good, and I will definitely make these again!  Great for Valentine's Day too!!  :-)

Okay, the good first: I have been using this recipe for mini cheesecakes for a while so I really like the taste and consistency. However, this recipe did not take me any where near 48 minis. More like 28.  Second,  1/2 cup of sugar is plenty sweet. text:
I have a very similar recipe to this one and they are sooo good and so easy to make. My son loves them but he's kinda picky so he like them plain without the cherrie topping. To make 12 mini cheesecakes you will need 1 8oz of cream cheese, 1/2 cup of sugar, 1 teaspoon of vanilla, 2eggs and 12 oreo cookies. You put cream cheese, sugar and vanilla and eggs in blender then spray your papercups put an oreo cookie in each one then the cheesecake mix and to the oven for 20min exact, let them cool put the cherry pie filling on top and to the fridge for a few hours. like i said very similar recipe but different cookie try them you will love them that is if you like cheesecake and oreos.

text:
I made this just as the recipe states.  It turns out PERFECT every time!!!  I always make different varieties.  I put one half pecan on top and drizzle chocolate on top; I use frozen strawberries; I leave a few plain and sprinkle a little of the wafer crumbs on top.  When I'm done with these varieties, I take oreo type cookies and crush a few for the crust, and coarsely chop some more.  I use the coarsely chopped to mix into the remaining cream cheese mixture and then also use some as a topping.  These little cheesecakes are quickly becoming a specialty of mine and are being requested by friends when they are coming for dinner!  Enjoy!

These were so much fun!  I haven't made cheesecake in years, so I was a little worried when I started making these. 

But, they turned out delicious!  I replaced the vanilla wafer with regular graham cracker crust (my favorite part of cheesecake!) and I used the regular sized muffin cups instead of the mini ones (mainly my eyes just skipped over the miniature word, but they still turned out great) 
I made some plain, and some with cherry filling.  I stuck them in the fridge a couple minutes after pulling them from the oven, and most all of them set very well. (I was having problems telling when they were done no thanks to my uneven oven...)

text:
This was my first cheesecake I ever made. I really enjoyed eating these. I used paper cupcakes liners which roughly made 17 mini cheesecakes. I took the advice of some people and just put one wafer in the cupcake (flat side down). Next time I will make the crust slightly more thicker. Needless to say, I still have (what feels like) a whole box full of the wafers. Someone did comment and wrote of an alternative gram cracker crust recipe, so I will try that sometime as well.

I cooked them for 15 minutes. When the timer is up, don't let them sit in the oven with the oven turned off because they will over bake and crack. The top center of the cheesecake did sink after cooling.

text:
I made this for my church group and got rave reviews! Crushed up some vanilla wafers and put them in regular-sized aluminum-foil muffin cups. Followed others' advice and put the muffin trays on a jelly roll sheet filled with boiled water on the bottom so that the wafer bottoms wouldn't burn. Put it in for 20 minutes. Cheesecake was perfect - light and deeeelicious! After letting it cool, I put a dollop of Cool Whip on each mini-cheesecake, layered thinly-sliced frozen strawberries on top, and drizzled some remaining strawberry juice on each cupcake. Refrigerate before serving -- sooooo yummy! Thank you Janice!!

text:
These were ok. I really wanted more of a thick, rich cheesecake taste. This was more of a out of the box cheesecake recipe to me.
I took the advice of other reviews and added mini chocolate chips to part of the batter. I used oreo cookie crumbs as the crust. Instead of buying a whole package of Oreos, it was cheaper to buy one of those ready made Oreos pie crusts on the cake/cookie isle of the grocery store. Each one is about 6 ounces. 
I also decided to go with graham cracker crumbs for the plain cheesecake crust. I mixed a little melted butter with it and they turned out great. 

My only complaint is that the batter be richer. I want to feel like I eating my days worth of fat grams in one incredible bite of cheesecake!

I am HORRIBLE at cooking let alone baking so when this recipe turned out AMAZINGLY DELICIOUS  cheesecakes I couldn't believe it. Kids wolfed them down in seconds! I did modify verrry slightly. I used crushed Chessman Cookies for the crust (because I love their taste) and I used regular cupcake baking pans because I didn't have mini's. If you use a standard size cupcake pan, the serving of 48 mini's actually makes 12 regular cheesecake cupcakes. I doubled the recipe and made 24......didn't last the night!

This recipe was quick and super easy! Definitely a keeper!

text:
These are ridiculously easy to make and quick to whip up. The recipe made exactly 48 mini cakes. I did not use the vanilla wafers I used a graham cracker crust because it's what I had on hand and what I prefer. I left the cheesecakes in their paper cups for serving. Key to this recipe looking extra presentable and uniform was piping the cheesecake mixture into the cups and tapping the pan gently to help it settle before placing them in the oven. I also placed a pan of boiling water in the oven under the muffin pan. This helped to prevent the cheesecake tops from cracking. Everyone was eating these by the handfuls, this recipe is definitely a keeper.

I love this recipe! I have made it several times for parties and my catering jobs and have had compliments every time. The only thing I do differently is use mini nilla wafers. These mini cheesecakes were AMAZING! Everyone who ate them at Christmas couldn't believe they were homemade! I will make these again and again :)

Couple things--if you are using a regular cup cake pan (not mini), the recipe will NOT yield 48 cheesecakes. I had to double the recipe for the filling and even then I only got about 36 total. Make these,you won't regret it!

This is a fun dessert, but I'm actually not sure I'll make it again. I'm not a huge fan of fruit filling, and think other cheesecake recipes would be better for mini cheesecakes. Note--I assumed "mini" just meant cupcake-sized cakes (which are, in fact, smaller than a normal cheesecake), whereas it actually refers to mini cupcake fillers. Keep this in mind when deciding how much you want to make, and what type of cupcake pans you own.

text:
I made these lovely treats for the Super Bowl gathering. Even though I was a first time cheesecake baker, the minis turned out perfect. 

Here are a few tips I collected from other reviewers and some of my own. Soften the cream cheese before mixing. Use blender to get rid off the smallest crumbs. Add cocoa and sugar to make chocolate minis or other different extracts for more flavors. Substitute for the graham cracker crust: 2.5 cups of crushed grahams + 8 tablespoons of melted butter + 8 spoons of white sugar (will try honey in limited quantities next time). I found 2 cups of graham crackers and 8 tablespoons of butter to be too buttery when cooked. Load each mini with about ¬æ tablespoon of the crust and press it down with fingers or find a utensil to fit the mini. I used the end of the ice cream scoop. Its end is flat and sized just a little smaller then the bottom of the cupcake liners. Use water bath and baked for about 12-13 min. No cracks, no sinking middle, no sticking to the paper liners, no broken crust! :)

text:
I have made this recipe many times in the past. I try to watch my sugar/fat intake, so I use the lowfat (not fat free) cream cheese and use Splenda in lieu of sugar. I crush up chocolate graham crackers and put about 1/2 Tablespoon in the bottom of a ramekin. I spoon in the filling. For a little added sweetness I take 1-2 Tablespoons of Polaner sugar free raspberry preservers, add just a little warm water, and stir it up with a spoon until I have a thick syrupy mixture. I spoon just a little on top of each cheesecake and swirl it around with the sharp end of a knife. I cook mine in a water bath in a 325 degree oven for 18-20 minutes. It makes a great dessert or anytime snack.

I made these for a friend's birthday and they were easy and great. I added cinnamon and nutmeg to the mixture and blended it well. I also found by the fruit section, a cream cheese fruit dip, which I used as a topping to the mini cheesecake. I then placed either one raspberry or one blackberry on top. It was a nice, fresh, and yummy treat - it also displayed very well. 

If you're travelling, then you'll want to put the fruit dip and berries on when you arrive to your destination.  

I had problems with the mini-muffin liners being too big, so I just sprayed extra baking spray and used toothpicks to free the cupcakes from the edges and then placed them in the mini-muffin liners.

Wow!!  I made these as a trial for a wedding that wants cheesecake cupcakes.  i didn't think the bride would be happy with my first attempt at the light cheesecake.  I literally dumped all the ingredients in a bowl and whipped for 2 minutes.  I then put the batter in Texas muffin sized tins on top of graham crusts.  I had to cook for about 25 - 30 minutes (larger size).  I topped some with whipped cream and choc. shavings, blueberry topping and even 2 tsp right out of the can of cherry pie filling.  Everyone gushed.  I had to try them - not heavy (big plus)  light and creamy.  The bride even asked if I could whip up another dozen to send to work with her hubby to get his and his co-workers reaction to them.  These are so easy I had the ready in 35 minutes - she took them home warm.  Bottom Line: Super easy, amazing taste, and it doesn't leave you feeling like you just ate the whole cheesecake rather than just one piece.

text:
I made these this past weekend. I used some of the suggestions from other reviews. 1st, I made a batch and I used the vanilla wafers. I just put the cookie in the cupcake paper, flat side down. I was a little worried about how that would go over but let me tell you, I will never make the crust again! I made the full size not the mini. They baked for 20 minutes. One thing that was great about using the cookie is, when you peel the cupcake wrapper off, it doesn't crumb all over! I also threw in a few handfuls of mini chocolate chips. Oh so good! Then I made another batch, using splenda instead of sugar. My husband has diabetes, so I needed to cut the sugar. Using the splenda, they tasted just as good. Next time I decide to make the sugar free batch, I think I will use a sugar free cookie. These will be very diabetic friendly!

I made these for a women's bible study christmas gift exchange party. They were all gone by the time it was time to leave :) These get a 5 star for taste but a 4 star for how many this recipe actually makes. Luckily i bought an extra bar of cream cheese or i wouldn't have had enough ( i still didn't have a lot but enough to do the job). I used 3 (8oz) bars of cream cheese, 3 eggs, and a little bit more sugar ( because of the extra cream cheese). I also used two cups of graham cinnamon and sugar cracker crumbs, 1stick of melted butter, and 1/4 cup of sugar for the crust.  With all that said i ended up with 20 1/2 mini cheese cakes so not even 2 dozen. I filled each cupcake liner with 1 tbs of the crust batter and pressed it down then i used 1/4 cup full of the cheese cake batter for each one so they turned out even. They were really good I just need to remember to double up the recipe if i want to make more than 12...

text:
These were pretty tasty and quick to make. I had to add more sugar because there was not a whole lot of flavor, but with a little more sugar, it became very sweet and tasty! However, clearly you were supposed to use the mini tins because when I changed the serving to 24 cakes, I thought it would make 12 regular sized cakes but it instead only made 8! I had to use a whole other brick on cream cheese to make a second batch. It was very disappointing. Also, you can not cream the sugar, cream cheese, eggs, and vanilla until fluffy all at once. You should most definitely cream the sugar and cream cheese first, then add the eggs and vanilla. The crust definitely needs butter as well! It is way too crumbly without any. However, despite the recipe's shortcomings, it was very delicious and every loved them, so I would make them again if given the chance.

I followed other suggestions of bringing cream cheese to room temperature, then beating to silky smooth and then gradually adding the eggs, sugar, and vanilla. For my first time making any type of cheesecake, I give 5 stars for ease.  However, I felt the taste was a little bland. The Nilla wafer crust was missing something?? I love cheesecake and the flavor of this was just ok.. Maybe it was the brand of cream cheese I used (Lucerne)??  I think next time I will add the lemon juice as suggested by others and probably do a grahm cracker or chocolate crust.  Most of the tops cracked but was hidden by the cherry topping.  And an entire box of Nilla wafers was WAY to much.. Maybe 1/3 of the box if you decide to go that route.

text:
Good cheesecake, I made a few changes. I used 1 and 1/4c of sugar and added 1/2c of greek yogurt for texture. Also used 1/3 less fat cream cheese. Substituted 1 of the eggs for 1/4c egg beaters. We have been dieting and wanted something sweet that doesn't ruin all our hard work. All in all very good. I suggest making sure the cream cheese is room temp and to beat it by itself first to remove any lumps.I added the yougurt then blended well. I added sugar by 1/2c measurements and tasted to see if it was sweet enough. Baked it for 20 mins in my oven. Good by itself doesnt even have to have a topping. We used a cinnamon snickerdoodle type of cookie insead of vanilla wafers.

text:
Great recipe.  I'm giving it a 4 because I did take a lot of the suggestions made by people here, rather than from the recipe itself.  I made 2 kinds: regular with strawberry and peanut butter.  I used a graham cracker base (with butter and sugar) for the regular ones, and an oreo cookie base (with just butter) for the peanut butter ones.  I made them regular-muffin sized, since I didn't have a mini-muffin pan.  Actually, I bought foil baking cups, which can stand up on their own, because I don't even have a regular muffin pan.

The regular ones with strawberry topping were made according to the recipe.  I made some strawberry sauce (frozen strawberries + sugar in a pot on medium/low heat until it reduces into a sauce) to put on top.  For the peanut butter ones, I melted some peanut butter chips in the microwave and mixed it in, then threw in another handful of peanut butter chips into the mix.

I had a bit of a problem with the baking, but it doesn't seem to weird, since I see other people had the same problems: crackling on the top, then the deflating in the middle.  I had put a pan of water underneath, which people had suggested to prevent this, but since it didn't work, next time I'll try it with a water bath.  The deflating didn't make too big of a problem, since I had the strawberry sauce to fill the dent, and the peanut butter chips kept the peanut butter ones fairly level.

I brought a bunch to work, and my co-workers loved them.  I even converted a guy who said he di

All of my friends and family absolutely love this recipe! It is 20X better than anything store bought!! I've made it numerous times now, here are some tips:
1. Make sure cream cheese is at room temp!!
2. I crushed up graham crackers for the crust, added some butter and pressed into liners.
3. Beat ingredients until light and fluffy, a couple minutes. No reason it should not be smooth, if lumpy keep beating it will get there!

text:
This was a very quick and easy recipe and perfect for parties.  I cut the recipe in half nad it made exactly one tray of 24 mini cheesecakes.  I followed another reviewer's instructions and left the vanilla wafer whole for the crust.  Some of them were a little hard to shove down into the bottom of the muffin cup, but they worked pretty well.  I noticed that when you use this method, the muffin paper gets flatter and wider (since the cookie is bigger around than the paper cup), so you end up with less area in the muffin cup for cheesecake.  This was not a problem, just an observation.  I used my usual cheesecake method (all ingredients at room temp, put a pan of water in the oven on the rack under the cheesecake for hydration of the air, and NEVER open the oven door to peek).  I got busy and didn't watch the oven, so they were just slightly cracking when I got back to them at the 15 minute timer which meant that they were overcooked.  Be sure to keep an eye on these!  They tasted a little gummy and heavy to me, but that as probably because I overcooked them.  I think next time I may try to just reduce my regular cheescake recipe down and see if that works out better, but these are good for a quick and easy (but not spectacular) party dessert.

text:
Mine came out really great! When i was mixing it...there were tiny little lumps but its all smooth and creamy when it came out of the oven! I suggest turning the oven off but leaving the cheesecakes in there after the required 15 minutes of baking. After about ten minutes, take it out of the oven and stick it in the fridge to cool. 
The wafers didnt turn out that good. it didnt really taste much liek vanilla and it made the bottom all oily and greesey. i suggest not using it! it would be just adding extra sugar, fat, and trans fat! 
The cheesecake tastes great with or without the topping. Without, you get more flavor of the creamy luxurious cheesecake. It would also taste better if you added a little bit more vanilla extract. 
This recipe is sooooo easy to make! its not time consuming at all and it tastes just like the real thing!

This was excellent and can easily be made ahead by one day.  I didn't put the cherry pie filling on top  until right before the party.  The recipe made 36 mini cheesecakes for me.  Will definitely make this again for get-togethers, etc...  You don't need the whole box of vanilla wafers (less than half will do and I still had leftovers) and I crushed them using my blender.  I did bake them using the mini liners.  I also followed the cheesecake tips and set the baking pan in a jelly roll pan that I filled with boiling water.  None of the cheesecakes cracked!

text:
Great recipe. Made the first time exactly as written except using graham cracker crust (roughly 12-16 full sz grahams run through food processor to make into crumbs; 7-8 tbsp butter melted combine and instead of pressing into muffin papers made into small balls and rolled and flattened then set into muffin wrapper...MUCH easier to get out of wrapper than the few I pressed) instead of nilla wafers just due to personal preference. 
2nd time around I tweaked a little :-) added a little lemon juice a little less sugar and 1/2 additional tsp vanilla and each time baked for approximately 17 minutes (do NOT wait until batter is cracking!) and then just turned off the oven and left for about 45 minutes to an hour. Cheesecakes turned out AMAZING! 
Couple tips-
-absolutely NEED cream cheese room temp!!!
-before adding anything else beat till as smooth as possible!
-add sugar beat again and again nice and smooth batter needed I can't emphasize that enough from years of making cheesecakes with mom and grandma
-add in eggs and beat until just mixed and then pour/scoop into cups :-)
SO many other possibilities/additions to make chocolate cheesecake or really whatever flavor you want! Will definitely keep making!!!! Thanks!

text:
I've made this recipe several times now.  My family really loves them!  They aren't too sweet, which is what my family enjoys. Most of my family like them plain without the cherry topping. When we make the very mini cheesecakes, we don't need anywhere near the recommended amount of vanilla wafers. (I made a half batch of 24 minature "minis" and did not use anywhere near 6 oz for the 1/2 batch. I only use the recommended 1/2 teaspoon per miniature muffin cup. Next time I'll try 2 or 3 ounces of Vanilla wafers crushed for a half batch.) We really enjoy the "mini" mini cheesecakes.  One bite desserts! Of course, everyone usually picks up one, walks away, then comes back for another. Very easy to make and everyone enjoys them!

text:
This was such a simple cheesecake to make. I've only made a no-make cheesecake before because I found baking a cheesecake intimidating. This was very easy and very tasty. 

I only made 3 changes to the original recipe. 1) I used a standard muffin/cupcake pan and cupcake liners. 2) I halved the recipe so that I wouldn't be alone with all that goodness. I was making this for only 2 people. Really, one because I'm on a diet. This yielded about 9 cupcakes. 3) I baked them for 15 minutes but they looked too loose, so I baked them for an additional 8 minutes. 

I let them cool and placed them in the fridge for about 2 hours. And then I topped them with the cherry pie filling/topping.

text:
I love these. There were a few false starts because I knew absolutely nothing about making cheesecake. I missed the miniature muffin tin part and had a hard time figuring out why my batch never made as many as the recipe said it should. I also had to cook mine a little longer since they were bigger which led to me over baking a few times which makes the mixture a little eggy.  They were still good, but you didn't get that rich creamy cheesecake texture or taste. You want there to still be a little jiggle in the middle. Once I got it down though, these were great. I bring them (as well as Paula Deen's sausage balls) to work potlucks and there are never any left over.

I followed some of the suggestions offered by other reviewers: let the cream cheese warm to room temperature before using (or heat it for 30 seconds-1 minute in the microwave), didn't completely crush the vanilla wafers (which helped them stick together better), and taking them out of the oven before they cracked (when possible). Rich, but not too sweet, these really are delicious! I'm excited to try them again but with other mix-ins.

text:
Delicious, easy recipe! I picked this since so many other cheesecake recipes required it to sit overnight - which probably does make it taste better, but even just eating after cooling it was still delicious. Another reviewer mentioned omitting the vanilla for lemon juice but instead I used one teaspoon of each - not sure what it did to the flavor, but the result was delicious. For the crust I used crushed oreos mixed with melted butter (to add a chocolate flair) - yum!  For sauce I pureed a cup of frozen raspberries then heated it on the stove with about 1/3 cup of sugar and a tablespoon of cornstarch - delicious fresh fruit topping alternative to jarred sauce!

This is my "go to" mini cheesecake recipe. You can't go wrong with this easy recipe. I save time by using whole cookies for my crust, either the mini round thin wafer cookies for my tassie pan or butter cookies/vanilla wafers/chocolate cookies for the muffin pan. So far, the best mini cheesecake recipe. I added 2 tbs of melted butter to the vanilla wafers crust. Also added 1 cup of melted white chocolate chips to the cheese batter, and so I reduced the amount of sugar to less than 3/4 cups so it won't get too sweet. Believe me, white chocolate gives the cheesecake an amazing flavor and creaminess. 
The second time I made two patches, one with Nella wafers and topped it with strawberries and blueberry, the second I added toasted coconut flakes and miniature Chocolat chips, with oreo crust. They are the best!

Brought to a July 4 BBQ.  Made a great presentation and everyone was impressed!  Delicious and easy!   Note regarding yield:  I got 48 mini (1-1/2") cheesecakes out of the batter.  I had a little batter leftover which was just enough for two regular muffin-size cheesecakes.  Topped half of them with strawberry pie filling and the other half with blueberry pie filling.  I only baked one tray at a time in the oven to make sure they baked evenly and I left them in 15 minutes.  Tip: Try to just use  mainly the fruit from the filling and less liquid to top each one... Since they are so small, you don't want the topping running over the edge and making a mess.

I put it in keblers mini graham cracker pans made enough for 6. equals to one package. I took it out let it cool for 10 minutes before I place it in the fridge for at least an hour . This method avoids cracking and dropping.

text:
This recipe is great as-is, though I've tried a few alterations with some success.  For one, if I have time, I use crushed graham crackers (Magic Bullet) with a little butter pressed into the cups and baked for 5 minutes to get them crustier.  And I just use raspberry, blueberry, and other jams/preserves -- more useful to have open jars of that in the fridge than unused cherry pie filling, though that tastes great too!  If your audience likes cheesecake, they'll love these!

text:
This was a fantastic recipe! I followed the recipe pretty close. I didn't have vanilla wafers but I did have un-frosted sugar cookies in the freezer so i put those in the food processor and used that for my crust. I used some of the suggestions in the reviews and put the eggs in one at a time and beat until fluffy. I had attempted in the past to make cheese cake and it turned out horrible, later I read all the things i did wrong. One of the things I learned from my last cheesecake disaster was to set your pan in water to even the baking. So I did that with these guys. Don't know if it made a difference, but they came out perfect! I made blueberry pie filling and used that for my topper. Very good recipe and will absolutely use this recipe again. Thanks for posting!

This recipe is soooo easy to make! Blend ingredients 2,3,4 & 5 with a mixer, it makes it very creamy. I make these for our church fish fry every year and they are gone before my husband can get to the dessert table.(I have to make a double batch each time because they go so fast.)Any fruit topping will do.
